Jamison Brereton

23 (319)
Indra (1тАУ7, 11), Indra or R╠еta (8тАУ10)
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The most salient feature of this hymn is the insistent series of questions that domi nate its first six verses. These questions all concern the sacrificersтАЩ relationship to IndraтАФwhich sacrificers have managed to attract and please Indra, how does Indra know who is sacrificing and where, who receives IndraтАЩs bounty and comradeship and by what means. A preliminary and oblique answer is given in the second half of verse 4: тАЬthe god will take cognizance of my truths,тАЭ that is, my praise and sacred formulations, which will ensure that Indra will come to our sacrifice and share his bounty. This answer is elaborated upon in the last verses of the hymn. After this partial answer in verse 4 the questions take on a more intimate tone, inquiring into the nature of IndraтАЩs friendship with his worshipers, who are now his comrades, whereas the first four verses were more concerned with the mechanics of attracting Indra to our particular sacrifice. A striking feature of these question verses is that, despite the poetтАЩs eagerness for the presence and intimate comradeship of Indra, the god is always referred to in the 3rd person, and indeed the poet and sacrificers are almost always in the 3rd person as well. This 3rd-person distancing of Indra reminds us somewhat of the doubts expressed about IndraтАЩs existence or at least his whereabouts in other R╠еgvedic hymns; the 3rd-person reference suggests that the poet has not established the direct personal contact with the god that he desires. Verse 7 serves as a transition to the amplified answers of verses 8тАУ10. In verse 7 Indra prepares to destroy тАЬthe lie,тАЭ the deceit that is inimical to the proper func tioning of the cosmos. After IndraтАЩs destruction of the lie, the ubiquitous and all-powerful force of тАЬtruthтАЭ can be celebrated in the remaining verses (8тАУ10, before the refrain verse 11). These three verses contain twelve instances of the word r╠еt├б тАЬtruth,тАЭ most of them initial in their p─Бda. As Paul Thieme illuminatingly pointed out (1964: 30), r╠еt├б is the implicit answer to the questions posed earlierтАФthe тАЬhow?тАЭ questions answered with тАЬby means of truth,тАЭ the тАЬwhich sacrificer?тАЭ questions by тАЬthe one who produces truth.тАЭ And we already saw that r╠еt├б as the answer was fore shadowed in the middle of the hymn (vs. 4cd). Thus we can satisfactorily resolve the apparent lack of connection between the first two-thirds of the hymn, with its bar rage of questions about Indra and the sacrifice, and the last third, with its insistently repeated тАЬtruthтАЭ and absolutely no mention of Indra, that led the Anukramaс╣З─л to suggest the possibility of two different divinities for the hymn (Indra 1тАУ7, 11; R╠еta 8тАУ10). Indra by destroying the lie (vs. 7) gave free rein to the workings of truth described in verses 8тАУ10.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra Thieme tr. and comments on this hymn in Gedichte (pp. 30-33).

рдорд╣рд╛рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдЧреБрдгреИрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдХрдерд╛ рдХрдердВ рдХреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рдЕрд╡реГрдзрддреН рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпреЗрддреН ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрдкреНрд░реЗрд░рд┐рддрд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░рд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рдорд╣рд┐рдореНрдиреЛрд╜рддрд┐рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рд╕ рдПрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╣реЛрддреБрдГ рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рдпрд╛рдЧрдВ рдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгрдГ рдкреНрд░реАрдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐ ред рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрджрд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрд░реБрдЪрд┐рддрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдКрдзрдГ рдЙрджреНрдзрддрдорддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдВ рд╕реЛрдордореН рдЕрдиреНрдзрдГ рд╕реЛрдорд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдВ рдкрд┐рдмрдиреН рдЖрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рджрдпрдиреН рдЙрд╢рд╛рдирдГ рддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдирдВ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЬреБрд╖рдорд╛рдгрдГ рд╕реЗрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╢реНрдЪ рдЛрд╖реНрд╡рдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╢реБрдЪрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рджреАрдкреНрддрд╛рдп рдзрдирд╛рдп рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдпред рдЙрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдзрдирдВ рдХрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рджрд╛рддреБрдВ рд╡рд╡рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╡рд╣рддрд┐ ред рдкреАрддрдореЗрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдирдВ рдЬрдард░реЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ред рдЕрдиреЗрди рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрджреНрд╡рдпреЗрди рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЪрд┐рдиреНрддреНрдпрдЪрд░рд┐рддрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐рддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn what manner may (any one) extol the mighty Indra? at the sacrifice of what worshipper may he, propitiated, be present, drinking the sacrificial Soma beverage, desirous of the (sacred) food, and plural ased (by the oblation)? the mighty Indra is borne (to the rite) for the purpose of bestowing brilliant wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How did he [=priest?] strengthen the great one [=Indra]? Enjoying the sacrifice of what HotarтАФ(coming) to the soma as to an udder,
eager for, enjoying, and drinking the stalkтАФhas he waxed high for the blazing stakes?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take p─Бda b as a complete clause, supplying a main verb (тАШkommtтАЩ Geldner, тАШgehtтАЩ Witzel Got┼Н). They then take the 2nd hemistich as a syntactically independent declarative sentence. Given the density of questions in the first 6 vss. of this hymn, I think a declarative sentence would be intrusive and therefore take bcd as part of the question begun with k├бsya in p─Бda a, with vavakс╣г├й in d as the main verb for the whole. On soma as an udder, see III.48.3 cited by both Oldenberg and Geldner

Note the close proximity of juс╣г─Бс╣З├бс╕е (b) and juс╣г├бm─Бс╣Зaс╕е (c). The latter is the only occurrence of this participle stem, while juс╣г─Бс╣З├б- is of course quite common. I don’t see any semantic nuance that would justify using two different stems here. I wonder if juс╣г├бm─Бс╣Зa- is a nonce to create a Behagel effect with the three nearrhyming and semantically similar stems: juс╣г─Бс╣З├│ тАж u┼Ы─Бn├│ juс╣г├бm─Бс╣Зo. It should also be evaluated in the context of the other anomalous and phonologically similar middle participles in this Indra cycle, including uс╣г─Бn├б- (IV.16.14), u┼Ы├бm─Бna- (IV.19.4), uс╣г├бm─Бna- (IV.22.2), and our own middle term uс╣г─Бn├бс╕е. (For disc. see esp. comm. ad IV.16.14.) Though uс╣г─Бn├б- is attested twice elsewhere, it is still problematic: though there is a root pres. to тИЪva┼Ы тАШbe eagerтАЩ with a zero-grade u┼Ы, the stem is otherwise only act. and the act. part. u┼Ы├бnt- is extremely well attested (see., e.g., the next hymns, IV.24.6b, 25.1b).

Geldner is adamant that the two verse-final datives ┼Ыucat├й dh├бn─Бya are not to be construed together. By contrast I think they belong together in principle. Of 6 occurrences of dh├бn─Бya (always p─Бda-final), 2 are preceded by mahat├й (I.104.7, IX.97.4), which modifies it. I am just somewhat uncertain what it refers. Although тИЪ┼Ыuc is generally an Agni root, and cf. ┼Ыu┼Ыuc─Бn├б- in the immediately preceding hymn, probably of Agni (IV.22.8), I think that referent is unlikely here. dh├бna- refers to the stakes in play or a prize or spoils, in this case presumably something Indra wants enough to exert himself for it. The verse has made abundantly clear what Indra wants most – soma (s├│mam b, ├бndhaс╕е c) – and I think it likely that soma is the referent here as well. A deriv. of тИЪ┼Ыuc, the adj. ┼Ы├║ci-, is regularly used of a type of soma (clear, as opposed to mixed), and the participle here may be expressing the same thing. I would therefore slightly emend the tr. to тАЬfor the gleaming stakes [=soma].тАЭ

Griffith

How, what priest’s sacrifice hath he made mighty, rejoicing in the Soma and its fountain?
Delighting in juice, eagerly drinking, the Lofty One hath waxed for splendid riches.

Geldner

Wie hat er den Gro├Яen erbaut? An welches Hotri Weihspruch fand er Gefallen und kommt zum Soma als zum Euter? Voll Verlangen trinkend, an dem Trank Gefallen findend ist er ├╝bergro├Я herangewachsen dem Ergl├╝henden zum Reichtum.

Grassmann

Wie doch und welches Priesters grosses Opfer liess er gedeihn, des Soma’s Euter liebend? Mit Lust geniessend, trinkend gern den Rauschtrank erwuchs zu hohem Reichthum der erhabne.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдВ рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджрдореН ред рд╕рд╣ рдорд╛рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджрдГ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордГ ред рддрдВ рд╕рд╣ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╡реАрд░рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдордорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╡реАрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдХрдГ рдкреБрдорд╛рдиреН рдЖрдк рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рдХрдГ рдЪ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рднрд┐рд░рдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдВрд╢ рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреЗ ред рдХрддреН рдХрджрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рдЪрд╛рдпрдиреАрдпрдВ рдзрдирдВ рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирд╕рдордпрдВ рди рдХреЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдЬрдирд╛рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрддреН рдХрджрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╢рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рддрдГ рдпрдЬреНрдпреЛрдГ рдпрд╖реНрдЯреБрд░реНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡реГрдзреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдирд╛рдп рдКрддреА рдКрддреНрдпрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рднреБрд╡рддреН рднрд╡реЗрддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhat hero has enjoyed his fellowship (in battle)? who has been a sharer in his benevolent thoughts? when does any one appreciate his wonderful bounty? when is he (presen) for the promotion of the prosperity of the man who glorifies and worships him?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

What hero has reached shared exhilaration with him? Who has attained it with his good favor?
Has his bright (course) appeared? Will he be here with help for the
strengthening of the one who has labored, eager to sacrifice?

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and Thieme (Gedichte 31) take the instr. sumat├нbhiс╕е as the object of s├бm ─Бnaс╣Г┼Ыa (e.g., Geldner тАЬWer wurde seiner Gnaden teilhaft?тАЭ), but this seems an unlikely use of the instr., even with the presence of the preverb s├бm – esp.

because the verb in b is essentially identical to the verb in a, ─Бpa, which takes the acc. Although Grassmann allows both acc. and instr. with s├бm тИЪna┼Ы in the sense тАШerlangenтАЩ, a careful perusal of the entry shows that this is the only instance with a supposed instr.; the others have the acc. I therefore supply the same obj. found in p─Бda a (sadham─Б╠Бdam) and take sumat├нbhiс╕е in normal instr. usage.

The second hemistich contains two occurrences of k├бd; the second is taken by all as simply a question marker, but Geldner interprets the first one as a full neut. with citr├бm, тАЬwelches Wunder?тАЭ This is possible, but it seems rhetorically better to take it as parallel in function to the other k├бd (so Thieme and Witzel Got┼Н as well as me). I supply тАШcourseтАЩ on the basis of II.34.10 citr├бс╣Г t├бd vo maruto y─Б╠Бma cekite тАЬThis bright course of yours, Maruts, appears ever more brightly,тАЭ also adduced by Geldner The notion of a journey is reinforced by the 2nd part of the hemistich. However, a tr. like Witzel Got┼Н тАЬIst sein Glanzzeichen bemerkt?тАЭ is certainly possible.

Griffith

What hero hath been made his feast-companion? Who hath been partner in his loving-kindness?
What know we of his wondrous acts? How often comes he to aid and speed the pious toiler?

Geldner

Welcher Mann hat ihn zum Zechgenossen bekommen? Wer wurde seiner Gnaden teilhaft? Welches Wunder von ihm hat sich gezeigt? Wird er zum Beistand, zur F├╢rderung des dienstbereiten Opferers geneigt sein?

Grassmann

Welch Held erlangte seine Tischgemeinschaft? und wer nahm Theil an seiner Huld und G├╝te? Wann zeigt sein Glanz sich? wann erscheint mit H├╝lfe zum Heile er dem eifervollen Opfrer?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHow is that Indra hears (the worshipper) who invokes him? and, hearing, how does he know his necessities? what are his gifts of old; why have they termed him the fulfiller (of the desires) of him who offers praise?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How does Indra hear (the call) being called? How, hearing it, does he know (the place for) his unhitching?
What are his many distributions (of goods)? How do they call him a provider for the singer?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Grassmann, Geldner, et al. take h┼лy├бm─Бnam to refer to the call or summons to Indra (e.g., Geldner тАЬWie h├╢rt Indra den Ruf?тАЭ). Kulikov (-ya-presents, 307-8) rejects this interpr., noting that this is the only instance of such a construction: normally the subject of the passive is the deity being invoked. Although he reluctantly admits that it might correspond to the rare transitive type in which what is spoken is the object of the verb (1.17.9), he prefers to derive this form from тИЪhu тАШpourтАЩ and translates тАЬHow does Indra hear the (libation) being offered?тАЭ – that is, the sound of the pouring. A different reconsideration is found in Witzel Got┼Н, who interpr. h┼лy├бm─Бna- in the standard way, as having the deity invoked as its subject – but they think Indra is listening to the summons to a different deity than Indra. Although I recognize that the standard interpr. may have glided too swiftly over the problems with h┼лy├бm─Бna-, the two revisionist versions both seem overelaborate and implausible to me. Since it is undeniable that forms of тИЪh┼л do sometimes take what is spoken as obj. (see the above-cited I.17.9, as well as juxtaposed occurrences of h├бvya- in VI.21.1 with comm. there), I think we must allow this rare usage in the passive as well, a point made very economically by Oldenberg My tr. follows that of Thieme (p. 31) тАЬWie h├╢rt Indra den [Ruf], der gerufen wird?тАЭ In b ├бvas─Бm is taken by all modern comm. and tr. as the gen. pl. of ├бvas- тАШhelpтАЩ that it appears to be. Although this gen. pl. is not otherwise attested (the only pl.

cases are nom./acc. and instr.), ├бvas─Бm is what the gen. pl. of this stem would be.

Moreover, it can easily be the complement of veda, which takes both acc. and gen. Nonetheless I favor GrassmannтАЩs interpr., that it is the acc. sg. of a root noun cmpd from ├бva тИЪs─Б тАШunhitchтАЩ. There is a major obvious stumbling block: the accent. Root noun cmpds are invariably accented on the final, so we expect *avas─Б╠Бm. However, the other putative ex. of this cmpd at III.53.20 has been mangled in transmission (see disc. by Scarlatta s.v. and comm. ad loc.), and I think it likely that the dominance of the тАШhelpтАЩ stem, which is remarkably well attested, led to a redactional change in accent.

One of the reasons I favor this solution has to do with the asya. In the тАШhelpтАЩ interpr., the asya would refer to the mortal who will receive this help (see Geldner n. 3b), but this hymn contains a lot of asyaтАЩs, and they all otherwise refer to Indra: 2a, 2b, 2c, 3c, 5c, 6c, plus enam 3d and asmin 5d. I very much doubt the poet would break this sequence with a pronoun referring to someone else. The only exception is asy─Б╠Б(с╕е) 5a, which is both accented and feminine, and is playing a trick by its patterning with the asya in 5c.

For ├║pam─Бti- from ├║pa тИЪm─Б тАШmete outтАЩ, see comm. ad VIII.40.9.

Griffith

How heareth Indra offered invocation? How, hearing, marketh he the invoker’s wishes?
What are his ancient acts of bounty? Wherefore call they him One who filleth full the singer?

Geldner

Wie h├╢rt Indra den Ruf? Wie wei├Я er, wenn er h├╢rt, ihm zu helfen? Welches sind seine vielen Zuwendungen? Wie kommt es, da├Я sie ihn den Beschenker des S├дngers nennen?

Grassmann

Wie h├╢ret Indra, was der Mensch ihm zuruft? wie kennt er h├╢rend, was den Menschen l├╢set? Und welche vielen Gaben schenket Indra? wie nennt man ihn des S├дngers reichen Spender?

Elizarenkova

рд╕рдмрд╛рдзрдГ рд╕рдкрддреНрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреАрдбрд╛рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рд╢рд╢рдорд╛рдирдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рджреАрдзреНрдпрд╛рдирдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдгрдВ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирдВ рдХрдерд╛ рдХрдердореН рдЕрднрд┐ рдирд╢рддреН рдЕрднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рдирдордГ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдВ рдЬрдЧреГрднреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐ рдЬреБрдЬреЛрд╖рддреН рдорд╛рдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╕реЗрд╡реЗрдд рддрджрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рди рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдореЗ рдорджреАрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЛрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдирд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╛ рднреБрд╡рддреН рднрд╡реЗрддреН ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд╕реНрдереЛ рдирдХрд╛рд░реЛрд╜рддрд┐рд╢рдпрд╡рд╛рдЪреА рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHow does he who glorifies Indra, and is diligent in his worship, although encountering opposition, obtain from him wealth? may the divine Indra be the appreciation of my praises, when accepting the sacrificial food he is propitiated towards me.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How will the man who has zealously labored and produced insights attain the material goods that belong to him [=Indra]?
The god will take cognizance of my truths, when he has accepted the homage that he will enjoy.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take d─л╠Бdhy─Бnaс╕е as parallel to ┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бn├бс╕е, referring to the verbal/mental work at the sacrifice as opposed to the physical – hence my tr. тАШproduced insightsтАЩ.

Other tr. seem to me to attenuate the semantics.

Griffith

How doth the priest who laboureth, ever longing, win for himself the wealth which he possesseth?
May he, the God, mark well my truthful praises, having received the homage which he loveth.

Geldner

Wie kann er, der eifrig den Opferdienst besorgt, seinen Reichtum erlangen, wie er ihn sich w├╝nscht? Der Gott nehme meiner rechten Worte wahr, die Huldigung annehmend, an der er seine Freude haben wird.

Grassmann

Wie doch erlangt, wer eifervoll ihm dienet, mit Andacht aufmerkt, seine G├╝terspende? Der Gott sei Zeuge meiner frommen Werke, ergreifend das Gebet, an dem er Lust hat.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhen, in what manner, at the dawning of this morning, has the divine Indra accepted the friendship of a mortal? when and in what manner, (is) his friendship (manifested) to the friends who have spread out the desirable and suitable (offering) before him?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How and what comradeship with a mortal does the god enjoy at the breaking of this dawn?
How and what is his comradeship for his comrades, who have tugged their well-harnessed desire to him?

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted above, fem. asy─Б╠Б(с╕е) patterns with the ubiquitous asya in this vs.: 5a kath─Б╠Бk├бd asy─Б╠Б/ 5c kath─Б╠Бk├бd asya.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we in any manner proclaim your friendship for your friends? when may (we make known) your fraternal regard? the efforts of the well-looking Indra are for the happiness of all; the wonderful form of the moving (Indra) is, like the sun, ever wished for.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Is his comradeship then a drinking vessel for his comrades? When will we proclaim his brotherhood to you?
The surges (of soma?) for him are a marvel, lovely to see for their beauty. He seeks (the milk?) from the cow, very bright like the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

─Б╠Бd is very rarely not in 1st position. Here the interrog. k├нm may have displaced it. See k├нm ─Б╠Бd at IV.30.7, as Geldner also notes, as well as тАж kuv├нd ─Б╠Бd I.33.1.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take the referent of te to be Indra (Geldner: тАЬWann d├╝rfen wir wohl von deiner Br├╝derschaft ├╢ffentlich sprechen?тАЭ). I very much doubt that. As I noted in the published introduction, Indra is always referred to in the 3rd ps. in this hymn, except in the final extra-hymnic V─Бmadeva refrain (vs. 11), and the thwarting of the poetтАЩs longing for intimacy by the distancing that the insistent 3rd ps. pattern imposes is in many ways the point of the hymn. I think it unlikely that the poet would introduce the intimate 2nd ps. reference through a single monosyllabic enclitic and then revert, in the next p─Бda, to the 3rd ps. asya. This leaves me with the problem of identifying an alternative referent for te. My assumption is that it is the poet speaking to himself, while the тАЬweтАЭ represents the collectivity of the ritual officiants. Alternatively, it is possible that te does refer to Indra and that this p─Бda represents a wistful wishful thinking about an intimacy not otherwise achieved – with its 1st ps. / 2nd ps. structure (the only place where a 1st ps. shows up in the hymn, save for the refrain – though see comm. on p─Бda d) and the particularly intimate relationship тАШbrotherhoodтАЩ (bhr─Бtr├бm) that is aimed at The second hemistich is problematic, primarily because of the form iс╣гa (Pp.

iс╣гe) in d. (Geldner characterizes it as тАЬdas zu den schwierigen Formen des с╣ЪV. geh├╢rtтАЭ), a problem compounded by the fact that its first syllable should, ideally, be heavy in this Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence. Before tackling it, we should consider the structure of the two p─Бdas. With Oldenberg and Witzel Got┼Н, but not Geldner, I take c and d separately, with c a nominal clause equating s├бrg─Бс╕е тАШsurgesтАЩ with v├бpuс╕е тАШmarvelтАЩ. In my view the surges consist of soma: s├бrga- is regularly used of soma in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX. Again with Oldenberg and Witzel Got┼Н, but not Geldner, I take sudс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыaс╕е as nom. pl. with s├бrg─Бс╕е, not gen. sg. – with ┼Ыriy├й construed with this adj.; cf. V.44.2 ┼Ыriy├й sudс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы─лс╕е. As for d, Oldenberg interprets iс╣гe as a 1st sg. тАЬsetze ich тАж in Bewegung,тАЭ with sv├аr с╣З├б citr├бtamam, standing for the surges in c, as its object. Witzel Got┼Н likewise take iс╣гe as a 1st sg. (aor. injunctive), but with the meaning тАШich sucheтАЩ, with the same obj. as Oldenberg By contrast I take it as a 3rd sg. (so also Geldner, it seems) and in fact would emend it (slightly) to *─лс╣гe (an asterisk should be inserted in the published translation), belonging to the perfect to the root given as тИЪeс╣г тАШsuchenтАЩ (etc.) by K├╝mmel (126-28). As was just noted, a heavy initial syllable would better fit the cadence; my one concern is that I do not understand why the short i was introduced. Though he does not include our form in his conspectus, K├╝mmel does list two other 3rd sg. med.

occurrences of this shape (─лс╣г├й X.89.3 and, with unclear root syllable, upeс╣г├й I.129.8).

He considers the pf. as resultative, and it is possible that my тАШseeksтАЩ should be changed to тАШhas soughtтАЩ. However, neither of his other examples (I.129.8, X.89.3) needs to be preterial, and so тАШseeksтАЩ may as well stay. The same emendation and semantic interpr. also work for iс╣гe in VI.22.5 and X.20.7; see disc. ad locc. What Indra is seeking here is, in my view, the milk to be mixed with the soma. It is characterized as тАЬvery bright like the sun,тАЭ and its source as тАШof/from the cowтАЩ (g├│с╕е or ─Б╠Бg├│с╕е) (─Б╠Бmay go with either *─лс╣гe or g├│с╕е). The slight disadvantage to my interpr. is that the two occurrences of ─Б╠Бg├│с╕е here and in the preceding hymn (IV.22.3) are construed differently, but given the convoluted structure in IV.22.3, that is probably unavoidable.

IV.23.7-10: The contrast between the тАШlieтАЩ (p─Бda-initial dr├║h- 7a) and с╣Ыt├б- (10 p─Бdainitial and 2 p─Бda-medial exx. in vss. 8-10) certainly underlines and cements the sense тАШtruthтАЩ for this word. Note also that с╣Ыс╣З─Б╠БтАШdebtsтАЩ, which opens the 2nd hemistich of vs 7, phonologically anticipates the с╣Ыt├бтАЩs to come.

рдЕрдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рджреНрд░реБрд╣рдВ рджреНрд░реЛрд╣рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдВ рдзреНрд╡рд░рд╕рдВ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рдХрд╛рдореН рдЕрдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдордЬрд╛рдирддреАрдВ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕реАрдВ рдЬрд┐рдШрд╛рдВрд╕рдиреН рд╣рдиреНрддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рддрд┐рдЧреНрдорд╛ рддрд┐рдЧреНрдорд╛рдирд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рддреАрдХреНрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдиреАрдХрд╛ рдЕрдиреАрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдЖрдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рддреБрдЬрд╕реЗ рддрджреНрд╡рдзрд╛рдп рддреЗрддрд┐рдХреНрддреЗ рдЕрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рддреАрдХреНрд╖реНрдгреАрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рдпрддреНрд░ рдпрд╛рд╕реВрд╖рдГрд╕реБ рддрджреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╣рдГрд╕реБ рдЛрдгрд╛ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЛрдгрд╛рдиреНрдпрдкрд┐ рдирдГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдмрд╛рдзрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрд╛рдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдЪ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрдмрд▓рдГ рдЛрдгрдпрд╛рдГ рдЛрдгрд╕реНрдп рд╣рдиреНрддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГред рдпрд╛рддрд┐рдГ рд╡рдзрдХрд░реНрдорд╛ ред рджреВрд░реЗ рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╛рдГ рдЕрдирдиреБрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рддреАрдГ рдмрдмрд╛рдзреЗ рдЕрдкреАрдбрдпрддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬResolving to kil the oppressing, malevolent (r─Бkс╣гasi), not acknowledging Indra, he sharpened his sharp weapons for (her) destruction, and the fierce (Indra) the canceller of debts, has kept afar the unknown dawns in which the debts (are to be paid).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Resolving to kill: jigh─Бс╣Гsan druham dhavarasam anindram: the implied r─Бkс╣гasi is thought to mean death, the debt of nature, the payment of what Indra’s favour delays by prolonging life

Jamison Brereton

Desiring to smash the lie, which is injurious and contrary to Indra, he sharpens the edges sharp for jabbing,
after the powerful avenger of debts has also thrust our debts far away to unknown dawns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tr. of t├йtikte, тАШsharpensтАЩ, may not seem to express its intensive semantics, but plain тАШsharpenтАЩ itself incorporates the iterative, repetitive motions of blade across stone that sharpening involves.

Geldner notes the similarity of с╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бcid to the root noun cmpd с╣Ыс╣Зa-c├нt- тАШcollector of debtsтАЩ found in the strikingly similar phrase II.23.17 s├б r╠ес╣Зac├нd rс╣З╠е ay─Б╠Б(с╕е). But there are no grounds to emend the phrase to a compound, though a deliberate echo seems possible. In fact changing the text here would have the disadvantage of eliminating the obvious object to bab─Бdh├й.

Griffith

About to stay the Indra-less destructive spirit he sharpens his keen arms to strike her.
Whereby the Strong, although our debts’ exactor, drives in the distant mornings that we know not.

Geldner

Um die Falschheit zu zerst├╢ren, die Fallen stellende, die keinen Indra kennt, sch├дrft er die scharfen Pfeilspitzen zum Angriff, w├дhrend der gestrenge Schuldvergelter unsere Schulden in die Ferne zu den unbekannten Morgenr├╢ten abgeschoben hat.

Grassmann

Die indra-lose t├╝ck’sche Druh zu t├╢dten, wetzt er zum Schiessen seine scharfen Pfeile, Wenn unsre Schuld der m├дcht’ge Schuldverfolger fernhin verbannt zu unbekannten Morgen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMany are the waters of с╣Ыta; the adoration of с╣Ыta destroys iniquities; the intelligent and brilliant praise of с╣Ыta has opened the deaf (ears) of man.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъta = sacrifice or truth or water; here it may apply to Indra, or to ─Аditya, or to the three former person nified divinities; the following verses are a succession of changes on the word

Jamison Brereton

Of truth there exist many riches. The vision of truth smashes the crooked,
and the signal call of truth bored open deaf earsтАФ(the signal call) of ─Аyu [=Agni], awakening and blazing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take the deaf ears to be those of ─Аyu – with ─Аyu referring to the ─Аrya in general, Witzel Got┼Н suggest. ─Аyu always poses difficulties, but in this case I think gen. ─Бy├│с╕е should be construed with ┼Ыl├│kaс╕е: the тАЬsignal call of ─Аyu,тАЭ referring to Agni and the sound of blazing fire. Elsewhere Agni is referred to as the тАЬlaud of ─АyuтАЭ (┼Ы├бс╣Гsa- ─Бy├│с╕е, IV.6.11, V.3.4), and this seems a similar expression referring to an audible product. The nom. participles budh─Бn├бс╕е ┼Ыuc├бm─Бnaс╕е тАШawakening, blazingтАЩ of course fit Agni very well. And it is not surprising, given his ritual role, that the sound of Agni should be considered to be identical to that of truth. As for the position of ─Бy├│с╕е, at some distance from ┼Ыl├│kaс╕е, note that it rhymes with ─Б╠Бg├│с╕е in 6d, likewise stationed at the end of the verse.

Griffith

Eternal Law hath varied food that strengthens; thought of eternal Law, removes transgressions.
The praise-hymn of eternal Law, arousing, glowing, hath oped the deaf ears of the living.

Geldner

Denn der Wahrheit Gaben sind viele: Die Erkenntnis der Wahrheit zerst├╢rt die Unredlichkeiten. Der Mahnruf hat die tauben Ohren des Ayu ge├╢ffnet, z├╝ndend, wenn er verstanden wird.

Grassmann

Denn vielfach sind des Opfers Labetr├дnke, des Opfers Andacht tilget die Vergehen; Des Opfers Ruf durchdrang die tauben Ohren des Menschenvolks, erweckend, hell erstrahlend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMany are the stable, sustaining, delightful forms of the embodied с╣Ыta; the с╣Ыta are (the pious) expectant of food; by с╣Ыta have the kine entered into the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e., as presents made to the officiating priests; the phrase may also mean, the rays of light have entered into the water, g─Бva с╣Ыtam ─Бvive┼Ыuс╕е ra┼Ыmay─Б udakam ─Бive┼Ыuс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Of truth the buttresses are firmly fixed; many are its gleaming marvels to be marveled at.
By truth the nourishments urge themselves along the long way, and by truth the cows approached truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tr. of d─лrgh├бm as extent of space, rather than GeldnerтАЩs extent of time (тАЬlange ZeitтАЭ), follows Thieme (p. 32): the nourishments as oblations go from earth to heaven, as rain from heaven to earth.

On irregular full-grade 3rd pl. vive┼Ыuс╕е see K├╝mmel (499-500).

Griffith

Firm-seated are eternal Law’s foundations in its fair form are many splendid beauties.
By holy Law long lasting food they bring us; by holy Law have cows come to our worship.

рдЛрддрдореН рдЛрддрджреЗрд╡рдВ рдпреЗрдорд╛рдирдГ рдирд┐рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╢реАрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛ рдЛрддрдорд┐рддреН рдЛрддрджреЗрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рд╡рдиреЛрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрднрдЬрддреЗ ред рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп рдЛрддрджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╢реБрд╖реНрдордГ рдмрд▓рдВ рддреБрд░рдпрд╛рдГ рддреВрд░реНрдгрдВ рдЧрд╡реНрдпреБрдГ ред рдЙ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ ред рдЬрд▓рдХрд╛рдорд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдмрд╣реБрд▓реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдг рдЧрднреАрд░реЗ рджреБрд░рд╡рдЧрд╛рд╣реЗ рдкреГрдереНрд╡реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЛрддрд╛рдп рдЛрддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдп рднрд╡рддрдГ ред рдзреЗрдиреВ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреМ рдкрд░рдореЗ рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЛрддрд╛рдп рдЛрддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдпреИрд╡ рджреБрд╣рд╛рддреЗ рджреЛрд╣рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рд╛рддреЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe (worshipper) subjecting с╣Ыta (to his will) verily enjoys с╣Ыta; the strength с╣Ыta is (developed) with speed, and is desirous of (possessing) water; to с╣Ыta belong the wide and profound heaven and earth; supreme kine, they yield their milk to с╣Ыta.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Desirous of possessing water: с╣Ыtasya ┼Ыuс╣гmas turay─Б u gavyuс╕е = ┼Ыuс╣гmo balam t┼лray─Бs t┼лrс╣Зam gavyuс╕е u carthe jalak─Бma┼Ыca bhavati

Jamison Brereton

(Whoever) holds fast to truth, just he wins truth. The explosive force of truth hastens swiftly as it seeks cattle.
For truth the two (worlds) are wide, ample, and deep; for truth do they, as the two highest milk-cows, give their milk.

Griffith

Fixing eternal Law he, too, upholds it swift moves the might of Law and wins the booty.
To Law belong the vast deep Earth and Heaven: Milch-kine supreme, to Law their milk they render.

Geldner

Wer an der Wahrheit festh├дlt, hat von der Wahrheit Gewinn. Der Drang der Wahrheit ist ein Renner, der Rinder erk├дmpfen will. F├╝r die Wahrheit sind beide Welten breit, ger├дumig, tief; f├╝r die Wahrheit geben sie als die vortrefflichsten Milchk├╝he ihre Milch.

Grassmann

Wer Opfer lenkt, der hat auch Lust am Opfer; des Opfers Kraft geht schnell und strebt nach K├╝hen; Dem Opfer str├╢men Milch die breiten, grossen, die tiefen, h├╢chsten beiden Welten-K├╝he.

English translation:

тАЬGlorified (in the past), glorified, Indra, at present, satisfy your worshipper with food, as rivers (are filled with water); lord of horses, a new hymn has been made for you; may we possessed of chariots, be ever diligent in our praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Now praised, o Indra, now being sung, make refreshment swell for the singer like rivers.
A new sacred formulation has been made for you, o you of the fallow bays. Through our insightful thought may we be charioteers who
always win.

Griffith

Now, Indra! lauded,- glorified with praises, let power swell high like rivers to the singer.
For thee a new hymn, Lord of Bays, is fashioned. May we, car-borne, through song be victors ever.

рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рдкрд░рддреНрд╡реЗрди рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреБ) (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реЗрдг рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕рддреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдкреНрд░рдж (рдиреБ) (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреН (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреБрдХрд╛рдп (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) (рддреЗ) (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдмреГрд╣рджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдзрдирдореН (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреЗ рдпрдерд╛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рд╕реБ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рдиреАрддрд┐рдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпреЗрдпреБрд╕реНрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╢реНрдиреЛрддреНрддрд░рдореИрддреНрд░реАрд╢рддреНрд░реБрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдгрд╕реЗрдиреЛрдиреНрдирддрд┐рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реЛрддреНрдХрд░реНрд╖рд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджрд╢рдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рдЬреЗ рддреБрдордЪреНрдпрд╛рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдиреАрддреА рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рдд рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреА рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реВрди рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдмрдиреВрди рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛. рее резрез рее
